    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

  <span id="freeText9311973907078278528" style="display:none">As Omega Point prepares to launch an all-out assault on The Reestablishment soldiers stationed in Sector 45, Adam's focus couldn't be further from the upcoming battle. He's reeling from his breakup with Juliette, scared for his best friend's life, and as concerned as ever for his brother James's safety. And just as Adam begins to wonder if this life is really for him, the alarms sound. It's time for war.<br /><br />On the battlefield, it seems like the odds are in their favor—but taking down Warner, Adam's newly discovered half brother, won't be that easy. The Reestablishment can't tolerate a rebellion, and they'll do anything to crush the resistance... including killing everyone Adam has ever cared about.<br /><br /><em>Fracture Me</em> sets the stage for <em>Ignite Me</em>, the explosive finale in Tahereh Mafi's epic dystopian series. Set during and soon after the final moments of <em>Unravel Me</em>, <em>Fracture Me</em> is told from Adam's perspective.</span>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I believe the order is:<br/>#1. Shatter Me<br/><br/>#1.5. Destroy me (novella, Warner's POV - optional, but I recommend reading it)<br/><br/>#2. Unravel Me<br/><br/>#2.5. Fracture Me (n<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I believe the order is:<br />#1. Shatter Me<br /><br />#1.5. Destroy me (novella, Warner's POV - optional, but I recommend reading it)<br /><br />#2. Unravel Me<br /><br />#2.5. Fracture Me (novella, Adam's POV - optional, you can read it, there are some bits that happen in between that help contextualise the background of things for the next novel)<br /><br />#3. Ignite Me<br /><br />I hope this helps :D<br /><br /><a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_526522456" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/526522456" />
    <a title="Cookie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7190378-cookie"><img alt="Cookie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483326823p2/7190378.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/526522456?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cookie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cookie" href="/user/show/7190378-cookie">Cookie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer526522456" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1631571100958357495">I figure since I already have this "preview," I might as well write a review for Addie Kent's novella.<br/><br/>AND LET ME TELL YOU, ADDIE SURPRISED ME SO SO MUCH. MY NOT-SO-POSITIVE OPINIONS ABOUT HIM HAVE, dare I say it, CHANGED.<br/><br/>When I thought I couldn't dislike him more than I did, after reading Fracture Me, Addie Kent proved me wrong. End of review.<br/><br/><b>Edit</b><br/>P.S.: Just because Adam didn't turn out to be your perfect little fucking angel with a perfect little fucking personality does not mean he was falsely </span>
  <span id="freeText1631571100958357495" style="display:none">I figure since I already have this "preview," I might as well write a review for Addie Kent's novella.<br /><br />AND LET ME TELL YOU, ADDIE SURPRISED ME SO SO MUCH. MY NOT-SO-POSITIVE OPINIONS ABOUT HIM HAVE, dare I say it, CHANGED.<br /><br />When I thought I couldn't dislike him more than I did, after reading Fracture Me, Addie Kent proved me wrong. End of review.<br /><br /><b>Edit</b><br />P.S.: Just because Adam didn't turn out to be your perfect little fucking angel with a perfect little fucking personality does not mean he was falsely portrayed. Shatter Me was written in FIRST PERSON LIMITED POINT OF VIEW, which means how Juliette sees Adam does NOT reflect the person that Adam IS. And don't give me the crap about how you clearly know Adam more than Tahereh Mafi does. For crap's sake, these are HER characters for crying out loud. FRACTURE ME is how Tahereh Mafi views Adam, so suck it up and move ON.<br /><b>Original</b><br />Chant with me guys. ANOTHER WARNER NOVELLA, WARNER NOVELLA, WARNER NOVELLA. SCREW ADAM (Adam who?)<br /><br />Update:<br />So according to <a href="http://www.harperteen.com/books/Fracture-Me-Tahereh-Mafi/?isbn=9780062284839" rel="nofollow noopener">Harper Collin</a>, this novella is titled Fracture Me (HA! We beat you to it Tahereh!) I don't know. Compared to Warner's title <b>Destroy</b> Me, which reflects just how strong W feels toward J, Fracture Me seems...weak.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2060909797" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11789843963454678518"><i>„Shit. This is even worse than I was expecting.“</i><br/><br/>Yes, that’s an actual quote from “Fracture me” and damn me if this wasn’t an adequate summary for the entire novella! *lol*<br/><br/><s>Give Adam a chance.</s><br/>I thought.<br/><br/><s>Maybe he isn’t all that bad.</s><br/>I was convinced.<br/><br/><s>Probably I misunderstood him the same way everyone misunderstood Warner at first.</s><br/>I kind of hoped.<br/><br/>… And then I read “Fracture me”.<br/><br/><u>
  <b>I was wrong!!!</b>
</u> <br/><br/>Adam is still a stupid moron and if anything the book just confirmed my initial suspicion. That boy is actua</span>
  <span id="freeText11789843963454678518" style="display:none"><i>„Shit. This is even worse than I was expecting.“</i><br /><br />Yes, that’s an actual quote from “Fracture me” and damn me if this wasn’t an adequate summary for the entire novella! *lol*<br /><br /><s>Give Adam a chance.</s><br />I thought.<br /><br /><s>Maybe he isn’t all that bad.</s><br />I was convinced.<br /><br /><s>Probably I misunderstood him the same way everyone misunderstood Warner at first.</s><br />I kind of hoped.<br /><br />… And then I read “Fracture me”.<br /><br /><u>
  <b>I was wrong!!!</b>
</u> <br /><br />Adam is still a stupid moron and if anything the book just confirmed my initial suspicion. That boy is actually as arrogant and dumb as I always thought him to be. He doesn’t believe in the rebels of Omega Point, he doesn’t believe in their cause, he doesn’t believe in Juliette! Hell! He even thinks she’s a retarded girl that doesn’t know what’s happening! <br /><br />How can anyone be so blind and self-righteous? <br /><br />Well anyway the only thing I liked about him was the fact that he truly seemed to care about James. But yes, that’s about it. <br /><br /><i>We hear the bombs explode far off in the distance, and that’s when I feel it: the bones inside of me fracture, little earthquakes breaking me apart.”</i><br /><br />Oh yeah and did I mention that once James was safe Adam didn’t even want to go looking for Juliette? I mean yes, he’s worried about his little brother, but damn he actually considered leaving her in the hands of the enemy??!!<br /><br />Logical conclusion: I HATE ADAM with a <u>
  <b>fierce passion!!!</b>
</u><br /><br />Words of wisdom: <br />If you’re already mad at him, don’t read the book. <br />You’ll only learn to hate him even more! *lol* ;-)</span>

<div id="review_529872680" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/529872680" />
    <a title="Mitchii" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4808951-mitchii"><img alt="Mitchii" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605348765p2/4808951.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/529872680?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mitchii" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mitchii" href="/user/show/4808951-mitchii">Mitchii</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4808951-mitchii?shelf=2013-standouts">2013-standouts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4808951-mitchii?shelf=dystopian-post-apocalyptic">dystopian-post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4808951-mitchii?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4808951-mitchii?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4808951-mitchii?shelf=action-adventure">action-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4808951-mitchii?shelf=2013-reads">2013-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4808951-mitchii?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4808951-mitchii?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4808951-mitchii?shelf=novellas-short-stories">novellas-short-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer529872680" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6186901705909638461">This novella for me is a revelation. It’s also a foreshadowing. It surprises me both in good and sad way. I’m very much vocal of my adoration towards Warner but I don’t have that much hate on Adam. I liked him just fine. The reason why I don’t prefer him is that he’s sort of bland. He doesn’t have much character and something’s telling me that he wasn’t the right guy for Juliette. Then <b>Destroy Me</b> and <strong>Unravel Me</strong> came that showed things that support my theory. But <b>Fracture Me</b>, ironically, which wa</span>
  <span id="freeText6186901705909638461" style="display:none">This novella for me is a revelation. It’s also a foreshadowing. It surprises me both in good and sad way. I’m very much vocal of my adoration towards Warner but I don’t have that much hate on Adam. I liked him just fine. The reason why I don’t prefer him is that he’s sort of bland. He doesn’t have much character and something’s telling me that he wasn’t the right guy for Juliette. Then <b>Destroy Me</b> and <strong>Unravel Me</strong> came that showed things that support my theory. But <b>Fracture Me</b>, ironically, which was told from Adam’s POV cemented it even more. I never would have guessed how fragile his feelings for Juliette were. I can’t even compare it to how he feels for James. Because if there’s only one person he needs to save, and between his little brother and woman she claimed he loved, I’m pretty sure, he—without a doubt—will save James. Don’t get me wrong, I admired his love for his brother but it just shows that she’s not his priority. He can even abandon her safety as long as the welfare of his brother is secured.<br /><br />(I think Adam earned some positive merit from me. He loves his brother and they have each other longer than he had Juliette. Of course, it is understandable that he wants his only family safety first. That doesn’t make his love for Juliette any less than what he really had for her. That’s actually the real question here: how much did he love her from the very start?)<br /><br />He doesn’t have a real inkling on what’s going on her mind. He doesn’t completely understand her and that’s why I think before that their relationship wouldn’t work. But what make it so unbearably sad is what Adam really thought of her—a weakling. I don’t entirely think of his words as insult (although it does sound kinda like it) but to describe a person in such negative context made me question his already questionable intentions. What he thought of her is the EXACT opposite of what Warner thinks of Juliette. He always pushes her forward, to embrace her potential, to make her understand that she is indeed strong. Whereas Adam wanted to baby Juliette, he even thinks that she’s going to weigh them down. I didn’t expect him to feel that way for Juliette, but it is without a shadow of doubt, true.<br /><br />In fact, I even saw more sincerity on Kenji. He was the one who was hell-bent on saving Juliette. He even blamed himself to what has happened. He’s the one reminding Adam that he should be worried, but no, he wanted to seize the momentarily peace they have and not stifle James safety unnecessarily. Now, tell me why should Juliette end up with Adam? Because I don’t see a single thing that will save his face with this revelation. Not even with the things he did in the first two books.<br /><br />It’s foreshadowing, that I can tell you. I don’t even need an image of Warner kissing Juliette (although will greatly appreciate) shoved to my face to know that they will be the end game. This novella pretty much solidified that. I have so much to say about their relationship but I’m saving it on my manifesto I’m writing for them (for my <a href="http://bookish.skycircus.org/2013/12/20/special-project-sixty-two-d-46/" rel="nofollow noopener">Project Sixty-Two</a> entry). But this novella definitely gave me the assurance I need.<br /><br />The story was bit shorter. It did bridge the gap between book 2 and 3. It wasn’t as personal as <b>Destroy Me</b>, and the one significant thing I learned from Adam is that he loves his brother so much. But also we got to know how things had happened prior to the opening chapter of <strong>Ignite Me</strong>. And by the looks of it, it promises amazing things to come. Yes, Juliette, remove those gloves, and go all out. I’m ending this review with my favorite quote from <b>Ignite Me</b>:<br /><blockquote>“<i>If there were even the slightest chance I could spare you this pain,” </i>he finally says, “<i>I would’ve taken it. You must know I wouldn’t have said it if it weren’t absolutely true.</i>” — Warner</blockquote><br />I’m so, <i>so</i> ready. I’m impatiently waiting here, and I have the feeling the wait will definitely pay off.<br /><br /><strong>4.5/5<br /><br />See original post here @ <a href="http://bookish.skycircus.org/2013/12/18/fracture-me/" rel="nofollow noopener">Aeropapers</a></strong><br /><br />****<br /><br />Post-Reading Comment:<br /><br />Let me clarify my rating first. <u>This doesn’t have anything to do with Adam</u>. And from the looks of it, it just cemented the reason why Warner and Juliette should be together. Actually, it solidify the end game here. Their understanding of the girl is contrasting, like night and day. It also showed who Adam main priority is; in a way told us who the most important person in his life is. And it ain't Juliette (not even himself). I was really surprised on how things went down in here. I didn’t expect Adam to be this callous and violent than necessary, or from what I know of him. <br /><br />I have tons to say but let me process all these thoughts in my head properly(it's wee hours of the night here). Adam gave me something to think about. Expect a lengthy review later. <br /><br />****<br /><br />See, I care for you Adam. I even changed the title, added the synopsis of your novella, and I even uploaded the cover. (11/03) Why so broken Adam? ;)<br /><br />****<br />Adam fans, this one's for all of you! ;) I'll still be reading you though. Don't worry. ;)<br /><br /><s>Is it too much to ask for another Warner Novella? Is it? *bribes mafi with cakes &amp; cookies* </s><br /><br />I'm just gonna sit here patiently and wait for Ignite Me! Warneeeer!!!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6186901705909638461" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1118739170" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1118739170" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1118739170?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=boring">boring</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=love-triangle">love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=short-story">short-story</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1118739170" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7802463009949860748"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1417320060i/12293110.jpg' width='400' height='230' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>My heart is fractured,<br/>broken,<br/>shattered,<br/>in pieces,<br/>for Adam.<br/><br/>Maybe I shouldn’t feel this way. Maybe he deserves it. He <em>was</em> an ass for most of the novella but, nevertheless, I cannot forget how good he once was for Juliette and how he obviously still cares for her.<br/><blockquote>
  <strong>I still want a future with her. I want to know that one day we’ll be able to settle somewhere safe and be together in peace. I’m not ready to give up on that dream yet. I’m not ready to give up on us.</strong>
</blockquote><br/>There’s one thing that I don’t like</span>
  <span id="freeText7802463009949860748" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1417320060i/12293110.jpg" width="400" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>My heart is fractured,<br>broken,<br>shattered,<br>in pieces,<br>for Adam.<br><br>Maybe I shouldn’t feel this way. Maybe he deserves it. He <em>was</em> an ass for most of the novella but, nevertheless, I cannot forget how good he once was for Juliette and how he obviously still cares for her.<br><blockquote>
  <strong>I still want a future with her. I want to know that one day we’ll be able to settle somewhere safe and be together in peace. I’m not ready to give up on that dream yet. I’m not ready to give up on us.</strong>
</blockquote><br>There’s one thing that I don’t like though: he thinks of her as a weak and irrational person AND is rude about it. I thought love was supposed to blind one from his/her true love’s imperfections? Or at least accept them.<br><br>That got me thinking. Is he really in love with Juliette? Or could it be that he dearly felt the necessity to protect her and keep her safe, because he loved how that made him and her feel? I’m still not sure about everything; my thoughts on him are a little disorganized for now.<br><br>What I do know though is that he has his qualities. He may not act as it would please us, readers, but his love for James was what saved his character in this novella for me.<br><blockquote>
  <strong>James clings to me, acting more like a child than he has in a long time, and I’m happy to see it. Sometimes I worry he’s growing up way too fast in this shitty world, and though I know I can’t protect him from everything, I still try. He’s been the only constant in my life for as long as I can remember; I think it’d rip me apart if anything happened to him.<br><br>I’ll never love anyone the way I love this kid.</strong>
</blockquote><br>I simply cannot resist brotherly love.<br><br>Many characters were present, except from Warner.<br><br>Yet he <em>felt</em> there. <em>Everywhere</em>. All the time. Adam was thinking how much he wants to slaughter him. Juliette’s confused feelings toward him were evident. And they were sort of panicked. Because he escaped.<br><br>The content of this novella is boring. Pertinent to some, but, unlike the #1.5 one, not as necessary/important. This is something that could have been only summarized – and I think it is briefly – in the third book.<br><br>You definitely don’t have to read this, only if you have some extra time in front of you. I did, because I was curious to know Adam’s opinion toward everything that happened, but it didn’t make me love him more or less. It just left me a bit unsatisfied and cofused concerning Adam’s real feelings for Juliette. And sad for everything that his character went through.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7802463009949860748" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3404698773468284059"><b>UPDATE:</b> SAY IT ISN'T SO! Adam's perspective? Really? Why in the world would you give Adam his own novella when you have WARNER (Warner!) whom you could write about. I mean, it's WARNER! Such a complex, tortured anti-hero. To say I'm disappointed is an understatement. Even Kenji would have been better than Adam.<br/><br/><b>UPDATE NOW THAT I'VE READ IT:</b> I don't know how you could want Juliette to end up with Adam after reading this. Just as <i>Destroy Me</i> showed me who Warner really is, <i>Fracture Me</i> has revealed t</span>
  <span id="freeText3404698773468284059" style="display:none"><b>UPDATE:</b> SAY IT ISN'T SO! Adam's perspective? Really? Why in the world would you give Adam his own novella when you have WARNER (Warner!) whom you could write about. I mean, it's WARNER! Such a complex, tortured anti-hero. To say I'm disappointed is an understatement. Even Kenji would have been better than Adam.<br /><br /><b>UPDATE NOW THAT I'VE READ IT:</b> I don't know how you could want Juliette to end up with Adam after reading this. Just as <i>Destroy Me</i> showed me who Warner really is, <i>Fracture Me</i> has revealed the true Adam, and it isn't pretty. He doesn't even really love her, at least not like Warner does, and Adam has zero chemistry with Juliette. Here's to hoping Tahereh Mafi wrote it this way to pave the way for Warner+Juliette!<br /><br /><br /><b>Original:</b><br />PLEASE, PLEASE be from Warner's POV.<br /><br />You know, you could include some Warner flashbacks to Chapter 62, too... I wouldn't complain or anything. =)</span>

"Fracture Me" was an okay read. I know it's not something i'll ever take the time to read again that's for sure.   <span id="freeText8278257407423762426" style="display:none"><u>3 I WILL NOT LOSE HER. ★'S</u> <br><br><i>“All I can think is how horrible and beautiful it is, that our eyes blur the truth when we can't bear to see it.”</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1521269490i/25226814._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Hmm... "Fracture Me" was an okay read. I know it's not something i'll ever take the time to read again that's for sure. There were a few sad bits like, the parts with Adam and his little brother James, and the loss of so many people and of course the loss of Omega Point. Things quickly go from bad to worse, and there was so much destruction and devastation in the wake of the battle against the Reestablishment. To say things ended horribly would be an understatement!! Anyways this novella is from Adams POV and to be honest it really didn't do much to improve his character. I really don't like him all that much. He doesn't believe in anything, NOT in the people of Omega Point, NOT in their cause and he sure as HELL doesn't believe in Juliette!!! Adam is so broody and is an annoyingly negative person, who whines way to freaking much for my taste. I cant stand how much he underestimates Juliette all the time, or the way he acts like she's a porcelain doll that can easily be broken, and the way he doubts her control of her powers and how deep down he's afraid of what her touch could do. I swear he acts as if he's better and could do a better job then everyone else. UGH!!! I say again, I do NOT like him! Adam is all kinds of wrong for Juliette. My feelings for Adam aside, I am glad I read it if only because it was nice getting insight into what happened after Juliette was taken by Anderson's men but I wish it was in Kenji POV instead. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1521269490i/25226814._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>“Every day we feel further apart. <div id="review_755045789" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/755045789" />
    <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library"><img alt="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350750103p2/4551536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/755045789?book_show_action=true">Nov 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=creepy-love-triangle">creepy-love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=amazing-writing">amazing-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=cover-lust">cover-lust</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=male-pov">male-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=failed-to-impress">failed-to-impress</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=reviewed-in-2013">reviewed-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=e-novella">e-novella</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer755045789" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2467099373864254772">Weird how things can change in very short periods of time! At the beginning of this series, there were Adam and Juliette, and I couldn’t imagine anything else. Then came Destroy Me, Warner’s novella that showed a whole new side of him, and (to my own surprise) I started thinking he might be a better choice for her after all. But my heart was breaking for poor Adam. I saw him as a nice and honest – if somewhat plain – boy, not strong enough and certainly not insightful enough to fully understand </span>
  <span id="freeText2467099373864254772" style="display:none">Weird how things can change in very short periods of time! At the beginning of this series, there were Adam and Juliette, and I couldn’t imagine anything else. Then came Destroy Me, Warner’s novella that showed a whole new side of him, and (to my own surprise) I started thinking he might be a better choice for her after all. But my heart was breaking for poor Adam. I saw him as a nice and honest – if somewhat plain – boy, not strong enough and certainly not insightful enough to fully understand someone as messed up as Juliette. <br><br>However, just like the previous novella, Fracture Me made me completely change my mind. In only 62 pages, Adam has managed to convince me that he’s so very wrong for her, and what’s more, that he doesn’t even really love her. Regardless of my past feelings for him, which was lukewarm at best, I didn’t expect to see this level of anger, jealously, and most of all, weakness. <br><br>The thing that troubles me most about Adam, his own doubts and reservations aside, is that he sees Juliette as someone in need of protecting, someone incapable of defending herself. Their relationship, as good as it might have seemed in the past, would never be a relationship of equals, never a true partnership. With Adam’s attitude, Juliette would never be free to grow to her full potential, she would always be kept back and sheltered. Unlike Warner, who keeps pushing her to be her best, even through nefarious means, Adam would wrap her in cotton and convince her she needs him – a big, strong soldier – to fight her battles.<br><br>Tahereh Mafi still does a wondrous job of adapting her writing to her POV character. It’s one of her greatest talents, I think, this ability to use writing as yet another tool for characterization. Adam’s narration is much like Adam himself – plain and a bit dry, with nothing distinctive about it. <br><br>Compared to Warner’s novella, Fracture Me is almost painfully short, but it contributes a lot to the series and sheds a very different light on Adam. I’m not sure how many fans he’ll have after this. If he ends up with Juliette after all, I for one I’m going to be very disappointed.<br><br>My three stars in no way reflect Tahereh’s writing and storytelling, which are brilliant. It’s more about the bitter disappointment this novella left me with, and it’s definitely a result of my strong dislike of Adam. I know I’ll be a sobbing mess after Ignite Me, though. Whichever way this goes, it can’t end well for everyone involved. Perhaps we should be smart about it and start a support group while there’s still time? <br>The clock is ticking, my friends. The heartbreak is almost here.<br><br><a href="http://www.thenocturnallibrary.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380226536i/681142.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2467099373864254772" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Ashwood (애쉬 우드)." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50173624-ashwood"><img alt="Ashwood (애쉬 우드)." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596432515p2/50173624.jpg" /></a>

<span id="freeTextContainer16058095126240308545">Hmm.. well, first off, just wanted to say Warner’s book was a million times better in my opinion🤔<br/><br/>This one made me not regret my decision of ‘not ever liking Adam again.’ <br/><br/>I liked the fact that he really loves and cares for James but I don’t like the fact that he’s always shutting him down and not letting him ask questions when, in their world being ignorant pretty much means death.   <span id="freeText16058095126240308545" style="display:none">Hmm.. well, first off, just wanted to say Warner’s book was a million times better in my opinion🤔<br /><br />This one made me not regret my decision of ‘not ever liking Adam again.’ <br /><br />I liked the fact that he really loves and cares for James but I don’t like the fact that he’s always shutting him down and not letting him ask questions when, in their world being ignorant pretty much means death. Kenji and Juliette are more than happy to answer any of James’ questions because they know what ignorance feels like. <br /><br />Adam’s ‘feelings’ for Juliette don’t move me because he wants to keep her ‘safe and sheltered’ instead of helping her control her powers and being a support system like Kenji, you can only hide for so long. So all that will do is keep her, in a way, crippled, always scared and only relying on constantly hiding. <br /><br />I’m glad he has James because at this point he can’t handle a girl in his life romantically or he just needs one that listens to everything he says, isn’t ambitious and one that doesn’t have any significant superpowers that she wants to actively use to help others. <br /><br />The thing that caused all the trouble between Adam and Juliette, was that she didn’t want to be the scared and submissive little girl she felt she had to be just to be accepted by the ppl around her, when she wanted to use her powers for something other than accidentally harming others, when she wanted to be a better, more confident version of herself, that’s when the trouble started between them. So, yea.. Adam can’t handle that type of female in his life. <br /><br />It literally broke my heart seeing how tore up and devastated Kenji was when he heard that Juliette was dead. He’s an amazing and loyal friend, love him to the moon and back🖤<br /><br />This story didn’t really add anything to the story for me but I did appreciate seeing what happened to Kenji during and after the attack, so that was worth the read. </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/699180568" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/699180568?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Prpages" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Prpages" href="/user/show/16586670-prpages">Prpages</a>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer699180568" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6995902366123016184">BEWARE THIS REVIEW HAS A LOT OF SPOILERS!!!<br/> My thoughts on this book are a matter of opinion. So if you're team Adam don't hate me. *Gives you cookies and Milk<br/><br/><br/>For the shorter version this book has managed to:<br/>A. Convince me that Adam is hiding something. Something we'll probably find out in Ignite Me.<br/>B. Confirm my belief that Juliette and Warner will be end game.<br/>C. That Kenji is, in fact-AWESOME. <br/>D. That Adam is not the bird. This is just a crackpot theory and I know he has the bird on his chest.</span>
  <span id="freeText6995902366123016184" style="display:none">BEWARE THIS REVIEW HAS A LOT OF SPOILERS!!!<br /> My thoughts on this book are a matter of opinion. So if you're team Adam don't hate me. *Gives you cookies and Milk<br /><br /><br />For the shorter version this book has managed to:<br />A. Convince me that Adam is hiding something. Something we'll probably find out in Ignite Me.<br />B. Confirm my belief that Juliette and Warner will be end game.<br />C. That Kenji is, in fact-AWESOME. <br />D. That Adam is not the bird. This is just a crackpot theory and I know he has the bird on his chest. But a lot of the story is centered around Juliette's personal growth. How she gets from point A to point B and the process of change she undergoes throughout the books. With that in mind I kind of think that maybe Warner's the bird. <br />Who got her out of the asylum? Adam was put into the asylum with her but who actually got her out?<br />Warner.<br />Who constantly throughout the books, is challenging Juliette to be stronger and better than she can be?<br />Warner.<br />And as far as we know he is also going to help her with her 'powers' and taking down the reestablishment. <br />Juliette has the capacity to be a really bad-ass character and I understand her anger towards Warner in the Ignite Me sampler. His father is supreme commander-who bombed the Omega Point and killed a lot of people. And the Kindness he's shown her doesn't make up for the time that she spent in sector 45 forced to be a 'weapon.' But I do think Warner is the bird. <br /> <br /><br />And now for the longer one:<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />One of the primary reasons I enjoyed this book is because it somehow managed to reaffirm my belief that Warner is right for Juliette. <br />Throughout the novella Adam is constantly looking down on Juliette. Afraid that she'll get hurt or end up costing them their lives. He is constantly looking at her as if she is a weak link, to scared and to fragile, to make her own decisions. I can admire his loyalty to James. But he is constantly looking at her in a negative light. Juliette can be annoying at times-granted. But the books are about Juliette finding her voice. Growing stronger, by herself. <br /><br />And You cannot grow stronger if you are constantly around someone who makes you weaker. <br /><br />Exhibit A: "It's hard for me to believe Juliette could hurt anyone like that."<br /><br />and: "Touching her is more serious than I ever thought it was." -Adam Kent (Taken out of context.)<br /><br />"Juliette has always been a little different from everyone else-she was like a crazed, skittish kitten when I first saw her in that cell-but she's been getting a lot better over the last few monthes." -Adam Kent<br /><br />"She's acting a lot like her old self right now."-Adam Kent (Taken out of context.)<br /><br />He's also a bit ignorant which isn't a problem, really. Tahereh Mafi does an excellent job at building suspense.<br /><br />Exhibit A: "He (Kenji) tried to break up a fight at the same time Juliette did, and bam, he went down in an instant. It was scary as hell-even though I know Juliette didn't mean to do it, there's really no other explanation. It had to have been her."-Adam Kent<br />(INSERT EYE ROLL HERE.)<br /><br />"Sometimes I think this whole movement is led by a bunch of idiots." -Adam Kent when thinking about Omega Point. I find it interesting that both Warner and Adam think the movement is idiotic. <br /><br />Tahereh Mafi even managed to work in a bit of Mean Girls: Exhibit A: "God, she's so obsessed with him."-Adam Kent when thinking about Juliette talking about Warner. <br /><br />*I applaud you Tahereh Mafi</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11762083461141498442">So, Adam is super lame, and now we have proof. Honestly, it was so blatantly obvious that he would make a horrible partner for Juliette, that I really cant see any way that Mafi can justify them being together now. There is no way that it can happen. I never really liked Adam. <div id="review_797098554" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=want-to-burn">want-to-burn</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=teenagers-with-powers">teenagers-with-powers</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=hero-boring">hero-boring</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=die-hero-die">die-hero-die</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer797098554" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6082422251091169149"><b>Spoilers</b><br/><br/>-What a manipulative novella. The only reason this was written was so readers would dislike Adam and switch to Team Psycho-Warner. In <i>Shatter Me</i> and <i>Unravel Me</i> Adam was crazy in love with Juliette, he risked his life for her and would have done anything for her. Yet in this, Adam didn't give a fuck about Juliette, he didn't even care that her life was at risk. Where did that come from? How did Adam's character become so inconsistent? <br/>The only reason Adam suddenly stopped being a perfect,</span>
  <span id="freeText6082422251091169149" style="display:none"><b>Spoilers</b><br /><br />-What a manipulative novella. The only reason this was written was so readers would dislike Adam and switch to Team Psycho-Warner. In <i>Shatter Me</i> and <i>Unravel Me</i> Adam was crazy in love with Juliette, he risked his life for her and would have done anything for her. Yet in this, Adam didn't give a fuck about Juliette, he didn't even care that her life was at risk. Where did that come from? How did Adam's character become so inconsistent? <br />The only reason Adam suddenly stopped being a perfect, devoted boyfriend and changed into an unappealing, disloyal loser was so that Warner would look good in comparison. I hate when authors write such manipulative shit. I'm not even Team Adam and I'm bloody pissed! Adam's feelings for Juliette changed overnight for no plausible reason whatsoever.<br /><br />-What the hell was with the 'I will not lose her' tag line on the cover — that wasn't even the case!! Adam was more than happy to lose Juliette, he didn't fight for her at all, even Kenji cared more about her welfare than flipping Adam.<br /><br />-I hope Juliette doesn't end up with Warner or Adam, it's dumb that all YA heroines have to choose their life long partner at age sixteen or seventeen.<br /><br />-The whole emphasis on Adam putting James first and loving him like no other made me roll eyes — it was as if the author was desperate to show that Juliette would never be first or mean as much as to Adam as his little brother. What a lot of rubbish. Someone loving a sibling and doing the best for them doesn't mean that they can't be in love with someone else and do their best for them too. <br />I wasn't buying Adam not wanting Juliette because he had to put his brother first — the author doesn't seem to realise that sibling love and romantic love are two very different things and a person can more than experience and respect both.<br /><br />-Ugh, I'm disgusted at how the author tried to manipulate readers in order to make Warner seem more suited to Juliette. It was so obvious that Adam was written in such an unflattering way for the sole purpose of making Warner look like the better match. <br /><br />-I would have preferred if Adam was written consistently instead of him having a sudden personality transplant… All just so that readers would see that he didn't understand or love Juliette like he should or like Warner did (who of course totally gets her *rolls eyes*) — there was no indication of Adam not understanding and loving Juliette in the first two books, they had a connection and they knew where the other was coming from. So yea, I didn't buy him being so uncaring and ignorant of all things Juliette in this.<br /><br />-All in all, this was bloody awful.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6082422251091169149" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('D751ojXLiykEZ8okDqspvlSDNkuMyw9y5ZsGxI/iRRRJSK6IsDAtzwJX0aecM4jiawhoYmIimWR5NK8IyPL8Bw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0Y/yVpu1fIGqiqy3ZOpxWLWo8+fIDOg5OUj2sruOcFGXeSl8Hk7aZ6y6tzT2ctAEiiOtziblfi+l519+/J7JQg==')})
  }

She was born in a small city somewhere in Connecticut and currently resides in Santa Monica, California with her husband, fellow author <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3046613.Ransom_Riggs' title='Ransom Riggs' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ransom Riggs</a>.   <span id="freeText8573653632852485402" style="display:none">Tahereh Mafi is the <i>New York Times</i> and <i>USA Today</i> bestselling author of the <i>Shatter Me</i> series. She was born in a small city somewhere in Connecticut and currently resides in Santa Monica, California with her husband, fellow author <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3046613.Ransom_Riggs" title="Ransom Riggs" rel="nofollow noopener">Ransom Riggs</a>. She can usually be found over-caffeinated and stuck in a book. <i>Shatter Me</i> is her first series, with television rights optioned by ABC Signature Studios; <i>Furthermore</i>, her first middle grade novel, is on shelves now, and <i>Whichwood</i>, its darker companion, will be on shelves November 14, 2017.</span>
